does not controvert our point,  so far at any rate as that it is the abolition of pain.

सोपप्लवस्य ज्ञानसंतानस्य बद्धत्वे निरुपलवस्य च मुक्तत्वे यो बद्धः स एव मुक्त इति सामानाधिकरण्यं न संगच्छते ।

But if you proceed to argue that the soul,  as being the cause of pain,

आवरणमुक्तिर्मुक्तिरिति जैनजनाभिमतोऽपि मार्गों न निसर्गतो निरर्गलः ।

is to be abolished just like the body,  &c. , we reply that this does not hold,

अङ्ग भवान्पृष्टो व्याचेष्टां किमावरणम् ।

since it fails under either alternative.  For do you mean by "the soul,"

धर्माधर्मभ्रान्तय इति चेदिष्टमेव ।

) something different therefrom?  (a. ) If the former,

अथ देहमेवाऽऽवरणम् ।

we make no objection,  [since we Naiyāyikas allow that cognition is evanescent,

तथा च तनिवृत्तौ पञ्जरान्मुक्तस्य भुकस्येवाऽऽत्मनः सततोर्ध्वगमनं मुक्तिरिति चेत्तदा वक्तव्यम् ।

[219] and we do desire to abolish cognition as a cause of pravṛitti or action[220]], for who would oppose a view which makes for his own side?  (b. ) But if the latter,

किमयमात्मा मूर्तोऽमूतों वा ।

then, since it must be eternal, [221] its abolition is impossible;

\* घ. पु. टि.\- कया युक्त्या ।

and, again,  a second objection would be that no one would try to gain your supposed "summum bonum;"

अत्यन्तगूढायितम् ।

for surely no sensible person would strive to annihilate the soul,  which is always the dearest of all,

+ घ. पु. टि.\- सामग्यभावे ।

on the [168]principle that "everything else is dear for the soul's pleasure;"  and, again,

प्रथमे निरवयवः सावयंवो वा ।

everybody uses such a phrase as "liberated,"  [and this very term refutes the idea of annihilation or abolition]. "But why not say with those Bauddhas who hold the doctrine of pure intelligence [i. e. , the Yogāchāras and the Sautrāntikas[222]], that 'the summum bonum' is the rising of pure intelligence consequent on the cessation of the conscious subject?"

निरवयवत्वे निरवयवो मूर्तः परमाणुरिति परमाणुलक्षणापत्त्या परमाणुधर्मवदात्मधर्माणामतीन्द्रियत्वं प्रसजेत् ।

To this view we object that there is an absence of means;  and also it cannot be established that the locus [or subject] of the two states is the same.

सावयवत्वे यत्सावयवं तदनित्यमिति +व्याप्तिबलेनानित्यत्वांपत्तौ कृतप्रणाशाकृताभ्यागमा निष्प्रतिबन्धौ प्रसरताम् ।

For the former,  if it is replied that the well-known fourfold set of Bauddha contemplations[223] are to be accepted as the cause,

अमूर्तत्वे गमनमनुपपत्रमेव ।

we answer that,  as [according to the Bauddha tenet of the momentary existence of all things] there cannot be one abiding subject of these contemplations,

चलनात्मिकाया: क्रियाया \* मूर्नत्वप्रतिबन्धात् ।

they will necessarily exercise a languid power like studies pursued at irregular intervals,  and be thus ineffectual to produce any distinct recognition of the real nature of things.

पारतन्त्र्यं बन्धः स्वातन्त्र्यं मोक्ष इति चार्वाकपक्षेऽपि स्वातन्त्र्यं दुःखनिवृत्तिश्चेदविवादः ।

And for the latter,  since the continued series of cognitions when accompanied by the natural obstacles[224] is said to be "bound,"

ऐश्वर्य चेत्सातिशयतया सहक्षतया च प्रेक्षावती नाभिमतम् ।

and when freed from those obstacles is said to be "liberated,"  you cannot establish an identity of the subject in the two states so as to be able to say that the very same being which was bound is now liberated.

प्रकृतिपुरुषान्यत्वख्याती प्रकृत्युपरमे पुरुषस्य स्वरूपेणावस्थानं मुक्तिरिति सांख्याख्यातेऽपि पक्षे दुःखोच्छेदोऽस्त्येव ।

Nor do we find the path of the Jainas,  viz. , that "Liberation is the releasing from all 'obstructions,'"

विवेकज्ञानं पुरुषाश्रयं प्रकृत्याश्रयं वेत्येतावदवशिष्यते ।

a path entirely free from bars to impede the wayfarer.  Pray, will our Jaina friend kindly inform us what he means by "obstruction"? [225] If he answers "merit,

तत्र पुरुषांश्रयामिति न श्लिष्यते ।

demerit, and error,"  we readily grant what he says.

पुरुषस्य कोटरथ्याँवस्थाननिरोधापातात् ।

But if he maintains that "the body is the true obstruction,  and hence Liberation is the continual upspringing of the soul consequent on the [169]body's annihilation,

नापि प्रकृत्याश्रयः ।

as of a parrot released from its cage,"  then we must inquire whether this said soul possesses form or not.

अचेतनत्वात्तस्याः ।

If it possesses form,  then has it parts or not?

किंच प्रकृतिः प्रवृत्तिस्वभाषा निवृत्तिस्वभावा वा ।

If it has no parts,  then, since the well-known definition of an atom will apply here as "that which has form without parts,"

आधेऽनिर्मोक्षः ।

it will follow that the attributes of the soul are,  like those of an atom,

स्वभावस्यानपायात् ।

imperceptible to the senses.  [226] If you say that it has parts,

द्वितीये संप्रति संसारोऽस्तमियात् ।

then the general maxim that "whatever has parts is non-eternal,"  would necessitate that the soul is non-eternal;

नित्यनिरतिशयसुखाभिव्यक्तिर्मुक्तिरित भट्टसर्वज्ञाद्यभिमतेऽपि दुःखनिवृत्तिरभिमतैव ।

and if this were conceded,  then two grand difficulties [against the Providential course of the world] would burst in unopposed,

परंतु नित्यसुखं न प्रमाणपद्धतिमध्यास्ते ।

viz. , that what the soul has done would,  at its cessation,

श्रुतिस्तत्र प्रमाणमिति चेन ।

perish with it [and thus fail of producing the proper fruit], while it would have reaped during life the effects of what it had not done [as the good and evil which happened to it would not be the consequences of its actions in a former birth]. If,  on the other hand,

योग्यानुपलब्धियाधिते तदनवकाशात् ।

the Jaina maintains that the soul does not possess form at all,  then how can he talk of the soul's "upspringing,"

अवकाशे वा ग्रावेप्लवेऽपि तथाभावप्रसङ्गात् ।

since all such actions as motion necessarily involve an agent possessing form? Again, if we take the Chārvāka's view "that the only bondage is dependence on another,

ननु सुखाभिव्यक्तिर्मुक्तिरिति पक्षं परित्यज्य दुःखनिवृत्तिरेव मुक्तिरिति स्वीकारः क्षीरं विहायारोचकग्रस्तस्य = सौवीररुचिपनुभावयतीति चेत्तदेवन्ना. टकपक्षपतितं त्वद्वच इत्युपेक्ष्यते ।

and therefore independence is the true liberation," —if by "independence" he means the cessation of pain,

सुखस्य सातिशयतयाँ सदृक्षतया बहुमत्यनीकाक्रान्ततया साधनप्रार्थनापरिक्लिष्टतया च दुःखाविनाभूतत्वेन विषानुषक्तमधुवदुःखपक्षनिक्षेपात् ।

we have no need to controvert it.  But if he means autocratic power,

नन्वेकमनुसंधिसतोऽपरं प्रच्यवत इति न्यायेन दुःखवन्सुरखमप्युच्छिद्यत इत्यकाम्योऽयं पक्ष इति चेन्मेवं मंस्थाः ।

then no sensible man can concede it,  as the very idea of earthly power involves the idea of a capability of being increased and of being equalled.

सुखसंपादने दुःखसाधनबाहुल्यानुषङ्गनियमेन तप्तायःपिण्डे तपनीयबुद्धया प्रवर्तमानेन साम्यापातात् ।

It is not consistent to say that it resides in the soul,  since the soul is held to be unchangeable,

तथाहि\- न्यायोपार्जितेषु विषयेषु कियन्तः सुखखद्योताः कियन्ति दःखदुर्दिनानि ।

and this would seem to involve that previously it had been hampered by ignorance;  nor can we say that it resides in nature,

\* घ. पु. टि.\-\-मूर्तसंबन्धात् ।

since nature is always held to be unintelligent.  Moreover,

= घ. पु. टि:\-\-आरनालक सौवीरमित्यमरः।

is nature spontaneously active or inactive?  If the former,

#### 4

चिन्तयितुं न शक्यमित्येतत्स्वानुभव मे प्रच्छादयन्तः सन्तो विदांकुर्वन्तु विदां वरा भवन्तः ।

then it follows that there can be no liberation at all,  since the spontaneous actions of things cannot be set aside;

तस्मात्परिशेषात्परमेश्वरानुग्रहवशाच्छ्रवणादिक्रमेणाऽऽत्मतत्त्वसा क्षात्कारवतः पुरुषधौरेयस्य दुःखनिवृत्तिरात्यन्तिकी निःश्रेयसमिति निरवद्यम् ।

and if the latter,  the course of mundane existence would at once cease to go on.

नन्वीश्वरसद्भात्रे किं प्रमाणं प्रत्यक्षमनुमानमागमो वा ।

Again, we have the same recognition of our "abolition of pain" in the doctrine of Bhaṭṭa Sarvajña and his followers,  that "Liberation is the manifestation of an eternal happiness incapable of being increased;"

न तावदत्र प्रत्यक्षं क्रमते ।

but here we have the difficulty that an eternal happiness does not come within the range of definite proof.  If you allege Śruti as the proof,

रूपादिरहितत्वेनातीन्द्रियत्वात् ।

we reply that Śruti has no place when the thing itself is precluded by a valid non-perception; [229] or if you allow its authority,

नाप्यनुमानम् ।

then you will have to concede the existence of such things as floating stones. "But if you give up the view that 'liberation is the manifestation of happiness,'

तद्वय सलिङ्गाभावात् ।

and then accept such a view as that which holds it to be only the cessation of pain,  does not your conduct resemble that of the dyspeptic patient who refused sweet milk and preferred sour rice-gruel?"

नाऽऽगमः ।

Your satire,  however, falls powerless,

विकल्पासहत्वात् ।

as fitter for some speech in a play [rather than for a grave philosophical argument]. The truth is that all happiness must [171]be included under the category of pain,  since, like honey mixed with poison,

किं नित्योऽवगमयत्यनित्यो वा ।

it is always accompanied by pain,  either as admitting of increase,

आद्येऽपसिद्धान्तापातः ।

[231] or as being an object of perception,  or as being exposed to many hostile influences,

द्वितीये परस्पराश्रयापतिः ।

or as involving an irksome necessity of seeking all kinds of instruments for its production.  Nor may you retort on us that we have fulfilled the proverb of "seeking one thing and dropping another in the search,"

उपमानादिकमशैक्यशङ्कम् | 'नियतविषयत्वात् ।

since we have abolished happiness as being ever tainted by some incidental pain,  and, at the same time,

तस्मादीश्वरः शशविषाणायत इति चेत्तदेतन्न चतुरचेतसां चेतसि चमत्कारमाविष्करोति ।

our own favourite alternative is one which no one can consider desirable.  For the truth is that any attempt to establish happiness as the summum bonum,

विवादास्पदं नगसागरादिकं सकर्तृकं कार्यत्वात्कुम्भवत् ।

since it is inevitably accompanied by various causes of pain,  is only like the man who would try to grasp a red-hot ball of iron under the delusion that it was gold.

ने चायमसिद्धो हेतुः ।

In the case of objects of enjoyment got together by rightful means,  we may find many firefly-like pleasures;

सावयवत्वेन तस्य सुसाधनत्वात् ।

but then how many are the rainy days to drown them?  And in the case of those got together by wrong means,

ननु किमिदं सावयवत्वम् ।

the mind cannot even conceive the future issue which will be brought about.  Let our intelligent readers consider all this,

अवयवसंयोगित्वमवयवसमवायित्वं वा ।

and not attempt to disguise their own conscious experience.  Therefore it is that we hold it as indisputable that for him,

नाऽऽद्यः ।

pre-eminent among his fellows,  who, through the favour of the Supreme Being,

गगनादौ व्यभिचारात् ।

has, by the regular method of listening to the revealed Śruti,  &c. , attained unto the knowledge of the real nature of the soul,

न द्वितीयः ।

for him the absolute abolition of pain is the true Liberation.  But it may be objected,

तन्तुत्वादावनैकान्त्यात् ।

"Is there any proof at all for the existence of a Supreme Being,  i. e. , perception,

तस्मादनुपपन्नमिति चेन्नैवं वादीः | समवेतद्रव्यत्वं सावयवत्वमिति निरुक्तेर्वक्तुं शक्यत्वात् ।

inference,  or Śruti?

अवान्तरमहत्त्वेन वा कार्यत्वानुमानस्य सुकरत्वात् ।

Certainly perception cannot apply here,  since the Deity,

नापि विरुद्ध हेतुः ।

as devoid of form,  &c. , must be beyond the senses.

साध्यविपर्ययंव्याप्तेरभावात् ।

Nor can inference hold,  since there is no universal proposition or true middle term which can apply.

नाप्यनैकान्तिकः ।

[232] Nor can Śruti,  since neither of the resulting [172]alternatives can be sustained;

पक्षादन्यत्र वृत्तेरदर्शनात् ।

for is it supposed to reveal,  as being itself eternal,

नापि कालात्ययापदिष्टः ।

or as non-eternal?  Under the former view an established tenet of our school would be contradicted [viz.

बाधकानुपलम्भात् ।

[233] As for comparison and any other proof which might be adduced [as that sometimes called presumption,  &c. ], they need not be thought of for a moment,

नापि सत्प्रतिपक्षः ।

as their object matter is definitely limited,  and cannot apply to the present case.

प्रतिभटादर्शनात् ।

[234] Therefore the Supreme Being seems to be as unreal as a hare's horn."  But all this elaborate disputation need excite no flurry in the breast of the intelligent,

ननु नगादिकमव र्तृकं शरीराजन्यत्वाद्गगनवदिति चेनैतत्परीक्षा क्षमभीक्ष्यते ।

as it can be at once met by the old argument,  "The mountain,

न हि कठोरकण्ठीरवस्य कुरङ्गे शात्रः प्रतिभटो भवति ।

seas, &c. , must have had a maker from their possessing the nature of effects just like a jar."  (a. ) Nor can our middle term [possessing the nature of effects] be rejected as unproved (asiddha), since it can be established beyond a doubt by the fact of the subject's possessing parts.

अजन्यत्वस्यैव ! समर्थतया शरीरविशेष\- वैदर्थ्यात् ।

"But what are we to understand by this 'possessing parts'? Is it 'existing in contact with parts,'  or 'in intimate relation with parts'? It cannot be the first,

तर्ह्य जन्यत्वमेव साधनमिति चेन्न ।

since this would equally apply to such eternal things as ether, [235] &c. ; nor can it be the second,

असिद्धेः।

since this would prove too much,  as applying to such cases as the [eternal] species,

नापि सोपाधिकत्वशङ्कनकलङ्काङ्कुरः संभवी ।

thread, which abides in intimate relation with the individual threads.  It therefore fails as a middle term for your argument."

अनुकूलतर्कसंभवात् ।

We reply,  that it holds if we explain the "possessing parts" as "belonging to the class of those substances which exist in intimate relation."

यद्ययमकर्तृकः स्यात्कार्यमपि न स्यात् ।

[236] Or we may adopt another view and [173]maintain that it is easy to infer the "possessing the nature of effects" from the consideration of their possessing intermediate magnitude. (b. ) Nor can our middle term be rejected as "contradictory" (viruddha),[238] since there is no such acknowledged universal proposition connected with it as would establish the opposite major term to that in our syllogism [i. e. , that they must have had no maker]. (c. ) Nor is our middle term too general (anaikānta), since it is never found in opposite instances [such as the lake,

इह जगति नास्त्येव तत्कार्य नाम यत्कारक चक्रमबंधी र्याऽऽत्मानमासादयेदित्येतदविवादम् ।

which is the vipaksha in the argument,  "The mountain has fire because it has smoke"]. (d. ) Nor again is it precluded (bādhita or kālātyayopadishṭa), for there is no superior evidence to exercise such a precluding power.

तच्च सर्वे कर्तृविशेषोपहितमर्यादम् | कर्तृत्वं चेतरकारकाप्रयोज्यत्वे सति सकलकारकमयोक्तुस्वलक्षणं ज्ञानचिकीर्षामयत्नाधारत्वम् ।

If you bring forward as an antagonistic syllogism,  "The mountains,

एवं च कर्तृव्यावृत्तेस्तदुपहित समस्तकारकव्यावृत्तावकारणककार्योत्पादप्रसङ्ग इति स्थूलः प्रमादः ।

&c. , cannot have had a maker,  from the fact that they were not produced by a body,

तथाँ निरटङ्कि शंकर किंकरेण— अनुकूलेन तर्केण सनाथे सात साधने ।

just as is the case with the eternal ether," —this pretended inference will no more stand examination than the young fawn can stand the attack of the full-grown lion;

साध्यव्यापकताभङ्गात्पक्षे नोपाधिसंभवः ॥

for the additional words "by a body" are useless,  since "from the fact that they were not produced" would be a sufficient middle term by itself [and the argument thus involves the fallacy called vyāpyatvāsiddhi]. [239] Nor can you retort,

#### 5

यदीश्वरः कर्ता स्यात्तर्हि शरीरी स्यादित्यादिप्रतिकूलतर्कजातं जागर्तीति चेदीश्वरसिद्धयसिद्धिभ्यां व्याघातः ।

"Well, let this then be our middle term;"  for you cannot establish it as a real fact.

आगमादेः प्रमाणत्वे बाधनादनिषेधनम् ।

Nor again is it possible to raise the [174]smallest shadow of a fear lest our middle term should be liable to limitation by any suggested condition (upādhi),[240] [such as "the being produced by a corporeal agent,"  to limit our old reason "from having the nature of effects"], because we have on our side a valid line of argument to establish our view,

आभासत्वे तु सैव स्यादाश्रयासिद्धिरुद्धता॥

viz. , "If the mountains,  &c. , had no maker,

#### 6

(न्या०कु०३।५) इति ।

then they would not be effects" [but all do acknowledge that they have the nature of effects], for in this world that is not an effect which can attain its proper nature independently of any series of concurrent causes.  And this series inevitably involves the idea of some sort of maker;

न च विशेषविरोधः शक्यशङ्कः ।

and I mean by "being a maker" the being possessed of that combination of volition,  desire to act,

ज्ञातत्याज्ञातत्वविकल्पपराहतत्वात् ।

and knowledge of the proper means,  which sets in motion all other causes,

स्यादेतत् ।

but is itself set in motion by none.  And hence we hold that if the necessity of a maker were overthrown,

परमेश्वरस्य जगन्निर्माणे प्रवृत्तिः किमर्था ।

the necessity of the action of all the other causes would be simultaneously overthrown,  since these are dependent thereon;

स्वार्था परार्था वा ।

and this would lead to the monstrous doctrine that effects could be produced without any cause at all.  There is a rule laid down by Śaṅkara-kiṅkara which applies directly to the present case—

आयेऽपीष्टप्राप्त्यर्थाऽनिष्टपरिहारार्था वा ।

"When a middle term is accompanied by a sound argument to establish its validity, "Then you cannot attempt to supply a limiting condition on account of the [supposed] non-invariable concomitance of the major term."

नाऽऽद्यः।

If you maintain that there are many sound counter-arguments,  such as "If the Supreme Being were a maker,

अवाप्तसकलकामस्य तदनुपपत्तेः ।

He would be possessed of a body,"  &c. , we reply,

अत एव न द्वितीयः ।

that all such reasoning is equally inconsistent,  whether we allow that Supreme Being's existence to be established or not.

द्वितीये प्रवृत्त्यनुपपत्तिः ।

As has been said by Udayana āchārya [in the Kusumāñjali, "If Śruti,

कः खलु परार्थ प्रवर्तमानं प्रेक्षावानित्याचक्षीत ।

&c. , have any authority,  your negative argument fails from being precluded;

अथ करुणया प्रवृत्त्युपात्तिरित्याचक्षीत कश्चित्तं प्रत्याचक्षीत ।

if they are fallacious,  our old objection of a 'baseless inference' returns stronger than ever."

तर्हि सर्वान्पाणिनः सुखिन एव सृजेदीश्वरः ।

Nor need we fear the possibility of any other contradiction to our argument,  since it would be overthrown by either alternative of God's being known or unknown.

न दुःखशबलान् ।

"Well, let all this be granted;  but the activity of God in creating the world,

करुणाविरोधात् ।

what end did it have in view?  His own advantage or some other being's? If it was for the former end,

स्वार्थमनपेक्ष्य परदुःखहाणेच्छा हि कारुण्यम् ।

was it in order to attain something desired,  or to avoid something not desired?

तस्मादीश्वरस्य जगत्सर्जन न युज्यते ।

It could not be the first,  because this would be quite incongruous in a being who possesses every possible desire gratified;

प्रयोजनमनुद्दिश्य न मन्दोऽपि प्रवर्तते ।

and for the same reason too it could not be the second.  If it was for the latter end [the advantage of another] it would be equally incongruous;

जगच्च सृजतस्तस्य किं नाम न कृतं भवेत् ॥

for who would call that being "wise" who busied himself in acting for another?  If you replied that His activity was justified by compassion,

#### 7

अत्रोच्यते ।

any one would at once retort that this feeling of compassion should have rather induced Him to create all living beings happy,  and not checkered with misery,

नास्तिकशिरोमणे तावदीकिषायिते चक्षुषी निमील्य परि. भावयतु भवान् ।

since this militates against His compassion;  for we define compassion as the disinterested wish to avoid causing another pain.

करुणया प्रवृत्तिरस्त्येव ।

Hence we conclude that it is not befitting for God to create the world."  This has been said by Bhaṭṭāchārya—

न च निसर्गतः सुखमयसर्ग: प्रसङ्गः ।

"Not even a fool acts without some object in view; "Suppose that God did not create the world,

सृज्यमाणिकृतसुकृतदुष्कृतपरिपाकविशेषाद्वैषम्योपपत्तेः ।

what end would be left undone by Him?" His action in creation is indeed solely caused by compassion;

न च स्वातन्त्र्यभङ्गः शङ्कनीयः ।

but the idea of a creation which shall consist only of happiness is inconsistent with the nature of things,  since there cannot but arise eventual differences from the different results which will ripen from the good or evil actions of the beings who are to be created.

स्वाङ्ग स्वव्यवधायकं न भवतीनि न्यायन प्रत्युत तनिर्वाहात् ।

Nor need you object that this would interfere with God's own independence [as He would thus seem to depend on others' actions], since there is the well-known saying,  "One's own body does not hinder one;"

एक एव रुद्रो न द्वितीयोऽवतस्थे (ले० सं० १। ८ । ६) इत्यादिरागमस्तत्र प्रमाणम् ।

nay rather it helps to carry out one's aims; [243] and for this there is authority in such passages of the Veda as that (in the Śvetāśvatara Upanishad,

यद्येवं तर्हि परस्पराश्रयबाधव्याधि समाधत्स्वोत चेत्तस्यानुत्थानात् ।

iii. 2), "There is one Rudra only;  he admits[244] not of a second,"

किमुत्पत्तौ परस्पराश्रयः शङ्कन्यते ज्ञप्तौ वा ।

&c. "But then how will you remedy your deadly sickness of reasoning in a circle?  [for you have to prove the Veda by the authority of God,

नाऽऽद्यः ।

and then again you have to prove God's existence by the Veda"]. We reply,  that we defy you to point out any reasoning in a circle in our argument.

आगमस्येश्वराधीनोत्पत्तिकत्वेऽपि परमेश्वरस्य नित्यत्वेनोत्पत्तेरनुपपत्तेः ।

Do you suspect this "reciprocal dependence of each,"  which you call "reasoning in a circle,"

नापिज्ञप्तौ ।

in regard to their being produced or in regard to their being known?  [245] It cannot be the former,

परमेश्वरस्योऽऽगमाधीनज्ञप्तिकत्वेऽपि तस्यान्यतोऽवगमात् ।

for though the production of the Veda is dependent on God,  still as God Himself is eternal,

नापि तदनित्यत्वज्ञतौ ।

there is no possibility of His being produced;  nor can it be in regard to their being known,

आगमानित्यत्वस्य तीवादिधर्मोपेतत्वादिना सुगमत्वात् ।

for even if our knowledge of God were dependent on the Veda,  the Veda might be learned from some other source;

तस्मानिवतकधर्मानुष्ठानवशादीश्वरप्रसादसिद्धावमिमतेष्टसिद्धिरिति सर्वमवदातम् ।

nor, again,  can it be in regard to the knowledge of the non-eternity of the Veda,

इति श्रीमत्सायणमाधवीये सर्वदर्शनसंग्रहेऽक्षपाददर्शनम् ॥

for the non-eternity of the Veda is easily perceived by [177]any yogin endowed with the transcendent faculties (tívra, Therefore,

#### 8

## c12

#### 0

अथ जैमिनिदर्शनम् ॥

THE JAIMINI-DARŚANA.

#### 1

ननु धर्मानुष्ठानवशादभिमतधर्मसिद्धिरिति जेगीयते भवता ।

An objector may here ask,  "Are you not continually repeating that merit (dharma) comes from the practice of duty (dharma), but how is duty to be defined or proved?"

तत्र धर्मः किंलक्षणकः किंममाणक इति चेदुच्यते ।

Listen attentively to my answer.  A reply to this question has been given in the older[247] Mímāṃsā by the holy sage Jaimini.

श्रूयतामवधानेन ।

Now the Mímāṃsā consists of twelve books.  [248] In the first book is discussed the authoritativeness of those collections of words which are severally meant by the terms injunction (vidhi), "explanatory passage" (arthavāda), hymn (mantra), tradition (smṛiti), and "name."

अस्य प्रश्नस्य प्रतिवचनं प्राच्यां मीमांसायां प्रादर्शि जैमिनिना मुनिना ।

In the second,  certain subsidiary discussions [as e. g. , on apúrva] relating to the difference of various rites,

सा हि मीमांसा द्वादशलक्षणी।

refutation of (erroneously alleged) proofs,  and difference of performance [as in "constant" and "voluntary" offerings]. In the third,

तत्र प्रथमेऽध्याये विध्यर्थवादमन्त्रस्मृतिनामधेयार्थकस्य शब्दराशेः प्रामाण्यम् ।

Śruti, "sign" or "sense of the passage" (liṅga), "context" (vākya), &c. , and their respective weight when in apparent opposition to one another,  the ceremonies called pratipatti-karmāṇi, things mentioned incidentally (anārabhyādhíta), things accessory to several main objects,

द्वितीये कर्मभेदोपोद्घातप्रमाणापवादप्रयोगभेदरूपोऽर्थः ।

as prayājas,  &c. , and the duties of the sacrificer.

तृतीये श्रुतिलिङ्गवाक्यादिविरोधप्रतिपत्तिकर्मानारभ्याधीतबहुप्रधानोपकारकायाजादियाजमानचिन्तनम् ।

In the fourth,  the influence on other rites of the principal and subordinate rites,

चतुर्थे प्रधानप्रयोजकत्वाप्रधानप्रयोजकत्वजुहूंपर्णतादिफलराजसूयगतजघन्याङ्गाक्षयूतादिचिन्ता ।

the fruit caused by the juhú being made of the butea frondosa,  &c. , and the dice-playing,

पञ्चमे श्रुत्यादिक्रमतद्विशेषवृद्ध्यवर्धनप्राबल्यदौर्बल्यचिन्ता ।

&c. , which form subordinate parts of the rājasúya sacrifice.  In the fifth,

षष्ठेऽधिकारितद्धर्मद्रव्यप्रतिनिध्यर्थलोपनप्रायश्चित्त सत्रदेयवह्निविचारः ।

the relative order of different [179]passages of Śruti,  &c. , the order of different parts of a sacrifice [as the seventeen animals at the vājapeya], the multiplication and non-multiplication of rites,

सप्तमे प्रत्यक्षवचनातिदेशशेषनामलिङ्गातिदेशविचारः ।

and the respective force of the words of Śruti,  order of mention,

अष्टमे स्पष्टास्पष्टप्रबललिङ्गातिदेशापवादविचारः ।

&c. , in determining the order of performance.  In the sixth,

नवम ऊहविचारारम्भसामोहमरोहतत्प्रसङ्गमगतविचारः ।

the persons qualified to offer sacrifices,  their obligations,

दशने बाधहेतुद्वारलोपविस्तारबाधकारणकार्थकत्वसमुच्चयग्रहादिसामप्रकीर्णनबर्थविचारः ।

the substitutes for enjoined materials,  supplies for lost or injured offerings,

एकादशे तन्त्रोपोद्घाततन्त्रावापतन्त्रप्रपञ्चनीवापप्रपश्चनचिन्तनानि ।

expiatory rites,  the sattra offerings,

द्वादशे प्रसङ्गन्तन्त्रिनिर्णयसमुच्चयविकल्पवि. चारः।

things proper to be given,  and the different sacrificial fires.

. तत्राथातो धर्मजिज्ञासेति ( जै० मू० १।१।

In the seventh,  transference of the ceremonies of one sacrifice to another by direct command in the Vaidic text,

१) प्रथममधिकरणं पूर्वमीमांसारम्भोपपादनपरम् ।

and then as inferred by "name" or "sign."  In the eighth,

अधिकरणं च पश्चावयवमाचक्षते परीक्षकाः ।

transference by virtue of the clearly expressed or obscurely expressed "sign,"  or by the predominant "sign,"

ते च पश्चावयवा विषयसंशयपूर्वपक्षसिद्धान्तसंगतिरूपाः ।

and cases where no transference takes place.  In the ninth,

तत्राऽऽचार्यमतानुसारेणाधिकरणं निरूप्यते ।

the beginning of the discussion on the adaptation of hymns when quoted in a new connection (úha), the adaptation of sāmans and mantras,  and collateral questions connected therewith.

स्वाध्यायोऽध्येतव्य इत्येतद्वाक्यं विषयः ।

In the tenth,  the discussion of occasions where the non-performance of the primary rite involves the "preclusion" and non-performance of the dependent rites,

चोदनालक्षणोऽर्थो धर्मः ( जै० सू० १।१।

and of occasions where rites are precluded because other rites produce their special result,  discussions connected with the graha offerings,

२ ) इत्यारभ्यान्याहार्ये च दर्शनात् ( जै० सू० १२।४।

certain sāmans,  and various other things,

४० ) इत्येतदन्तं जेमिनीयं धर्मशास्त्रमनारभ्यमारभ्यं वेति संदेहः ।

and a discussion on the different kinds of negation.  In the eleventh,

अध्ययनविधेरदृष्टार्थत्वदृष्टार्थत्वाभ्याम् ।

the incidental mention and subsequently the fuller discussion of tantra[249] [where several acts are combined into one], and āvāpa [or the performing an act more than once]. In the twelfth,  a discussion on prasaṅga [where the rite is performed for one chief purpose,

तत्रानारभ्यमिति पूर्वः पक्षः ।

but with an incidental further reference], tantra,  cumulation of concurrent rites (samuchchaya) and option.

अध्ययनविधेरर्थावबोधलक्षणदृष्टफलकत्वानुपपत्तेः ।

Now the learned describe a "topic" as consisting of five members,  and these are (a. ) the subject,

अर्थावबोधार्थमध्ययनविधिरिति वदन्वादी प्रष्टव्यः\-किमत्यन्तमप्राप्तमध्ययनं विधीयते किंवा पाक्षिकमवघातवनियम्यत इति ।

(b. ) the doubt,  (c. ) the primâ facie argument,

न तावदाद्यः।

(d. ) the demonstrated conclusion,  and (e. ) the connection (saṅgati). The topic is discussed according to the doctrines held by the great teachers of the system.

यनमर्थावबोधहतुरध्ययनत्वाद्भारताध्ययनवदित्यनुमानेन विध्यनपेक्षतया प्राप्तत्वात ।

Thus the "subject" to be discussed is the sentence,  "The Veda is to be read."

अस्तु तर्हि द्वितीयो यथा नख विदलनादिना तण्डुलनिष्पत्तिसंभवात्पाक्षिकोऽवघातोऽवश्यं कर्तव्य इति विधिना नियम्यते ।

Now the "doubt" which arises is whether the study of Jaimini's śāstra concerning duty,  beginning with the aphorism,

तथा लिखितपाठे. नार्थज्ञानसंभवा\-पाक्षिकमध्ययनं विधिना नियम्यत इति चेन्नैतच्चतुरस्रम् ।

"Duty is a thing which is to be recognised by an instigatory passage,"  and ending with "and from seeing it in the anvāhārya,"

दृष्टान्तदान्तिकयोधर्म्यसंभवात् ।

is to be commenced or not.  The primâ facie argument is that it is not to be commenced,

अवघातनिष्पन्नैरेव तण्डुलैः पिष्टपुरोडाशादिकरणेऽवान्तरापूर्वद्वारा दर्शपूर्णमासौ परमापूर्वमुत्पादयतो नापरथा।

whether the injunction to read the Veda be held to have a visible and present or an invisible and future fruit.  (a. ) If you say that this injunction must have a visible fruit,

अतोऽपूर्वमवघातस्य नियमहेतुः ।

and this can be no other[250] than the knowledge of the meaning of what is read,  we must next ask you whether this said reading is enjoined as something which otherwise would not have been thought of,

प्रकृते लिखितपाठजन्येनाध्य यनजन्येन वाऽर्थावबोधेन क्रत्वनुष्ठानसिद्धेरध्ययनस्य नियमहेतुनास्त्येव ।

or whether as something which otherwise would have been optional,  as we see in the rule for shelling rice.

तस्मादर्थावबोधहेतुविचारशास्त्रस्य वैधत्वं नास्तीति ।

Well, then,  let it be the latter alternative;

तर्हि श्रूयमाणस्य विधेः का गतिरिति चेत्स्वर्गफलकोऽक्षरग्रहणमात्रविपिरिति भवान्परितुष्यत ।

just as the baked flour cake called puroḍāsa is made only of rice prepared by being unhusked in a mortar,  when, but for the injunction,

विश्वजिन्न्यायेनाश्रुतस्यापि स्वगस्य कल्पयितुं शक्यत्वात् ।

it might have been unhusked by the finger-nails.  There, however,

यथा स स्वर्गः सर्वान्प्रत्यविशिष्टत्वात् ( जै.. सू. ४।३।

the new moon and full moon sacrifices only produce their unseen effect,  which is [181]the principal apúrva,

१३ )इति विश्वजित्यश्रुतमप्यधिकारिणं संपादयता तद्विशेषणं स्वर्ग: फलं युक्त्या निरणायि तद्वदध्ययनेऽप्यस्तु ।

by means of the various minor effects or subordinate apúrvas,  produced by the various subordinate parts of the whole ceremony;

तदुक्तम्\-: . ___ विनाऽपि विधिना दृष्टलाभान्न हि तदर्थता ।

and consequently the minor apúrva of the unhusking is the reason there for the restricting injunction.  But in the case which we are discussing,

#### 2

कल्प्यस्तु विविसामर्थ्यात्स्वर्गो विश्वजिदादिवत् ॥

there is no such reason for any such restriction,  as the rites can be equally well performed by gaining the knowledge of the Veda's meaning by reading a written book,

#### 3

एवं च सति वेदमधीत्य स्नायादिति स्मृतिरनुगृहीता भवति ।

or by studying under an authorised teacher.  Hence we conclude that there is no injunction to study the Púrva Mímāṃsā as a means of knowing the sense of the Veda.

अत्र हि वेदा. ध्ययनसमावर्तनयोरव्यवधानमवगम्यते ।

(b. ) "What,  then, becomes of the Vedic injunction,

तावके मते त्वधीतेऽपि वेदे धर्मविचाराय गुरुकुले वस्तव्यम् ।

'The Veda is to be read'?" Well,  you must be content with the fact that the injunction will have heaven as its [future] fruit,

तथा सत्यव्यवधानं बांध्येत ।

although it merely enjoins the making oneself master of the literal words of the Vedic text [without any care to understand the meaning which they may convey], since heaven,  though not expressly mentioned,

तस्माद्विचारशा. स्त्रस्य वैधत्वाभावात्पाठमात्रेण स्वर्गसिद्धेः समावर्तनशास्त्राच्च धर्मविचारशास्त्रमनारम्भणीयमिति पूर्वपक्षसंक्षेपः।

is to be assumed as the fruit,  according to the analogy of the Viśvajit offering.

सिद्धान्तस्त्वन्यतः प्राप्तत्वादमाप्तविधित्वं माऽस्तु ।

Just as Jaimini,  in his aphorism (iv.

नियमविधित्वपक्षस्तु वज्रहस्तेनापि नापहस्तयितुं पार्यते ।

3, 15), "Let that fruit be heaven,  since it equally applies to all,"

तथाहि\-स्वाध्यायोऽध्येतव्य इति तव्यप्रत्ययः प्रेरणापरपर्यायां पुरुषप्रवृत्तिरूपार्थभावनामाव्यामभिवाभावना\* प्रत्याययति ।

establishes that those who are not expressly mentioned are still qualified to offer the Viśvajit sacrifice,  and infers by argument that its characteristic fruit is heaven,

सा ह्यर्थमायनी भाव्यमाकाङ्क्षति ।

so let us assume it to be in the present case also.  As it has been said—

न तावत्समानपदोपात्तमध्ययनं भाव्यत्वेन परिरमते ।

"Since the visible fruit would be equally obtained without the injunction,  this cannot be its sole object;

अध्ययन शब्दार्थस्य स्वाधीनोचारणक्षमत्वस्य वाङ्मनसव्यापारस्य क्लेशार्थकस्य नाव्यत्वासंभवात् ।

we must rather suppose heaven to be the fruit from the injunction's significance,  after the analogy of the Viśvajit,

नापि समानवाक्योपात्तः  स्वाध्यायः ।

&c." Thus,  too, we shall keep the Smṛiti rule from being violated:

स्वाध्यायशब्दार्थस्य वर्णराशेनित्यत्वेन विभुत्वेन चोत्पत्त्यादीनां च. तुर्णा क्रियाफलानामसंभवात् ।

"Having read the Veda,  let him bathe."

तस्मात्सामर्थ्यप्राप्तोऽवबोधो भाव्यत्वेनावतिष्ठते ।

For this rule clearly implies that no long interval is to take place between reading the Veda and the student's return to his home;  while, according to your opinion,

अर्थी समर्थों विद्वानधिक्रियत इति न्यायेन दर्शपूर्णमासादिावधयः स्वविषयावघोधमपेक्षमाणाः स्वार्थबोधे स्वाध्यायं विनियुञ्जते ।

after he had read the Veda,  he would still have to remain in his preceptor's house to read the Mímāṃsā discussions,

अध्ययनविधिश्च लिखितपाठादिव्यावृत्त्याऽध्ययनसंस्कृतत्वं स्वाध्यायस्यावगमयति ।

and thus the idea of no interval between would be contradicted. ) that the study of Mímāṃsā is not enjoined,

तथा च यथा दर्शपूर्णमासादिजन्यं परमापूर्वमवघातादिजन्यस्यावान्तरापूर्वस्य कल्पकं तथा समस्तक्रतुजन्यमपूर्वजातं क्रतुज्ञानसाधनाध्ययननियमजन्यमपूर्वं कल्पयिष्यति ।

(b. ) that heaven can be obtained by the simple reading of the text,  and (c. ) that the rule for the student's return to his home is thus fulfilled,

नियमादृष्टानिष्टौ विधिश्रणवैफल्यमापयेत ।

we maintain that the study of the Mímāṃsā discussions on duty is not to be commenced.  The "authoritative conclusion" (siddhānta), however,

न च विश्वजिन्न्यायेन फलकल्पनाऽवकल्प्यते ।

is as follows: We grant that it cannot be a case of vidhi,

अर्थावबोधे दृष्टे फले सति फलान्तरकल्पनाया अयोगात् ।

for it might have been adopted on other grounds;  but not even Indra with his thunderbolt could make us lose our hold of the other alternative that it is a case of niyama.

लभ्यमाने फले दृष्टे नादृष्टफलकल्पना ।

In the sentence,  "The Veda is to be read,"

विधेस्तु नियमार्थत्वान्नाऽऽनर्थक्यं भविष्यति ॥

the affix tavya expresses an enforcing power in the word, [252] which is to be rendered visible by a corresponding action in man,

#### 4

ननु वेदमात्राध्यायिनोऽर्थावबोधानुदयेऽपि साङ्गवेदाध्यायिनः पुरुषस्यार्थावबोघसंभवाद्विचारशास्त्रस्य वैफल्यमिति चेत्तदसमञ्जसम् ।

bringing a certain effect into existence;  and this enforcing power seeks some corresponding end which is connected with the man's creative effort.

बोधमात्रसंभवेऽपि निर्णयस्य विचाराधीनत्वात् ।

Now it cannot be the act itself of reading,  as suggested by the whole word adhyetavya,

तद्यथा\- अक्ताः शर्करा उपदधाति ( तै० ब्रा० ३\-१२\-५) इत्यत्र घृतेनैव न तैलादिनत्ययं निर्णयो व्याकरणेन निगमेन निरुक्तेन वा न लभ्यते ।

which it thus seeks as an end;  for this act of reading,

विचारशास्त्रेण तु तेजो वै घृतमिति वाक्यशेषवशादर्थनिर्णयो लभ्यते ।

thus expressed by the word,  could never be regarded as an end,

तस्माद्विचारशास्त्रस्य वैधत्वं सिद्धम् ।

since it is a laborious operation of the voice and mind,  consisting in the articulate utterance of the portion read.

न च वेदमधीत्य स्नायादिति शास्त्रं गुरुकुलनिवृत्तिपरं व्यवधानप्रतिबन्धकं बाध्येतेति मन्तव्यम् ।

Nor could the portion read,  as suggested by the whole sentence,

स्नात्वा भुङ्क्त इतिवत्पूर्वापरीभावसमानकर्तृकत्वमात्रप्रतिपत्त्याऽध्ययनसमावर्तनयो रन्तर्याप्रतिपत्तेः।

be regarded as the end.  For the mass of words called "Veda,"

तस्माद्विधिसामर्थ्यादेवाधिकरणसहस्रात्मकं पूर्वमीमांसाशास्त्रमारम्भणीयम् ।

which is what we really mean by the words "portion read,"  being eternal and omnipresent,

इदं चाधिकरणं शास्त्रेणोपोद्घातत्वेन संबध्यते ।

could never fulfil the conditions of the four "fruits of action,"  production,

चिन्तां प्रकृतसिद्धयर्थामुपोद्घातं प्रचक्षते ॥

&c. [253] Therefore the only true end which remains to us is the [183]knowledge of the meaning,  as obtained by carrying out the sense of the words of the injunction.

#### 5

• इदमेवाधिकरणं गुरुमतमनुसृत्योपन्यस्यते\-अष्टवर्ष ब्राह्मणमुपनयीत तमध्यापयीतेत्यत्राध्यापनं नियोगविषयः प्रतिभासते ।

According to the old rule,  "He has the right who has the want,

नियोगश्च नियोज्यमपेक्षते ।

the power,  and the wit,"

कश्चात्र नियोज्य इति चेदाचार्यककाम एव ।

those who are aiming to understand certain things,  as the new and full moon sacrifices,

इत्यादिना पाणिन्यनुशासनेनाऽऽचार्य के गम्यमाने नयतेर्धातोरात्मनेपदस्य विधानात् ।

use their daily reading to learn the truth about them.  And the injunction for reading,

उपनयने यो नियोज्यः स एवाध्यापनेऽपि ।

since it virtually excludes the reading of written books, , so the mass of apúrva produced by all the sacrifices necessitates and establishes a previous apúrva produced by the restricting injunction (niyama), which prescribes reading the Veda as the means to know how to perform these sacrifices.

तयोरेकप्रयोजनत्वात् ।

If you hesitate to concede that a niyama could have this future influence called apúrva,  the same doubt might equally invalidate the efficacy of a vidhi [as the two stand on the same level as to their enjoining power]. Nor is the supposition a valid one that heaven is the fruit,

उपनीय तु यः शिष्यं वेदमध्यापयेदिङ्गः ।

according to the analogy of the Viśvajit offering,  since, if there is a present and visible fruit in the form of a knowledge of the meaning of the sacred text,

साङ्गं च सरहस्यं च तमाचार्य प्रचक्षते ।

it is improper to suppose any other future and unseen fruit.  Thus it has been said—

#### 6

ततश्चाऽऽचार्यकर्तृकमध्यापनं माणवककतृकेणाध्ययनेन विना न सिध्यतीत्यध्यापनविधिप्रयुक्त्यैवाध्ययनानुष्ठानं सेत्स्यति ।

"Where a seen fruit is obtained,  you must not suppose an unseen one;

प्रयोज्यव्यापारमन्तरेण प्रयोजकन्यापारस्यानिर्वाहात् ।

but if a vidhi has the restricting meaning of a niyama,  it does not thereby become meaningless."

त_ध्येतव्य (तै० आ०२।१५) इत्यस्य विधित्वं में सिध्यतीति चेन्मा सैत्सीत्का नो हानिः ।

But an objector may say,  "Although a man who reads the simple text of the Veda may not attain to a knowledge of its meaning,

पृथगध्ययनविधेरभ्युपगमे प्रयोजनाभावात् ।

still, as he who reads the Veda with its aṅgas,  grammar, &c. , may attain to this knowledge,

विधिवाक्यस्य नित्यानुवादत्वेनाप्युपपत्तेः ।

the study of Mímāṃsā will be useless."  But this is not true:

तस्मादध्ययनविधि' मुपजीव्य पूर्वमुपन्यस्तौ पूर्वोत्तरपक्षी प्रकारान्तरेण प्रदर्शनीयौ।

for even though he may attain to a simple knowledge of the literal meaning,  all deeper investigation must depend on this kind of discussion.

विचारशास्त्रमवैधत्वेनानारब्धव्यमिति पूर्वपक्षो वैधत्वेनाऽऽरब्धव्यमिति राद्धान्तः ।

For instance,  when it is said,

तत्र वैधत्वं वदता वदितव्यं किमध्यापनविधिर्माणवकस्यार्थावबोधमपि प्रयुङ्क्ते किंवा पाठमात्रम् ।

"He offers anointed gravel,"  neither grammar nor nigama[254] nor nirukta will determine the true meaning that it is to be anointed with ghee and not with oil,

नाऽऽद्यः ।

&c. ; it is only by a Mímāṃsā discussion that the true meaning is unravelled from the rest of the passage,  "Verily, ghee is brightness."

विनाऽप्यर्थावबोधेनाध्यापनसिद्धः।

[255] It is therefore established that the study of Mímāṃsā is enjoined.  Nor need it be supposed that this contradicts the passage of Smṛiti,

न द्वितीयः ।

"Having read the Veda,  let him bathe,"

पाठमात्रे विचारस्य विषयप्रयोजनयोरसंभवात् ।

which implies that he should now leave his teacher's house,  and prohibits any further delay;

आपाततः प्रतिभातः संदिग्धोऽर्थो विचारशास्त्रस्य विषयो भवति ।

as the words do not necessarily imply that the return to the paternal roof is to follow immediately on his having read the Veda,  but only that it is to follow it at some time,

तथा सति यत्रीर्थावग: तिरेव नास्ति तत्र संदेहस्य का कथा ।

and that both actions are to be done by the same person,  just as we see in the common phrase,

विचारफलस्य निर्णयस्य प्रत्याशा दूरत एव ।

"Having bathed,  he eats." Therefore from the purport of the injunction we conclude that the study of the Púrva Mímāṃsā Śāstra,

तथा च यदसंदिग्धमप्रयोजनं न च तत्प्रेक्षावत्मतिपित्सागोचरैः ।

consisting of a thousand "topics," [256] is to be commenced.

समनस्केन्द्रियसंनिकृष्टः स्पष्टालोकमध्यमध्यासीनो घट इति न्यायेन विषयप्रयोजनयोरसंभवेन विचारशास्त्रमनारभ्यमिति पूर्वः पक्षः।

I now proceed to give a sketch of the discussion of the same "topic" in accordance with the teaching of the Guru Prabhākara.  In the Smṛiti rule,

#### 7

अध्यापनविधिनाऽर्थावबोधो मा प्रयोजि ।

[258] "Let him admit as a pupil the Brahman lad when eight years old (by investing him with [185]the sacred cord), let him instruct him,"  the object of the direction appears to be the pupil's instruction.

तथाऽपि साङ्गग्वेदाध्यायिनो गृहीतपदपदार्थसंगतिकस्य पुरुषस्य पौरुषेयेष्विव प्रबन्धेष्वान्नायेऽप्यर्थावबोधः प्रामोत्येव ।

Now a direction must have reference to somebody to be directed;  and if you ask who is here to be directed,

ननु यथा विषं भुक्ष्वेत्यत्र प्रतीयमानोऽप्यों न विवक्ष्यते माऽस्य गृहे भुक्था इति भोजनप्रतिषेधस्य मातृवाक्यतात्पर्यविषयत्वात् ।

I reply, "He who desires to be a teacher,"  since, by Pāṇini's rule (i. 3, 36), the root ní is used in the ātmanepada when honour,

तथाऽऽम्नायार्थस्याविवक्षायां विषयावभावदोषः प्राचीनः प्रादुःध्यादिति चेन्मेवं  घोषः ।

&c. , are implied,  i. e. , here the duty which a teacher performs to his pupils.

दृष्टान्तदाष्टन्तिकयौपम्यसंभवात् ।

He who is to be directed as to admitting a pupil is the same person who is to be directed as to teaching him,  since both are the object of one and the same command.

विषभोजनवाक्यस्याऽऽतमणीतस्वेन मुख्यार्थपरिग्रहे षाधः स्यादिति विवक्षा नाऽऽधीयते ।

Hence the inspired sage Manu has said (ii.  140), "The Brāhman who girds his pupil with the sacrificial cord and then instructs him in the Veda,

अपौरुषेये तु वैदे प्रतीयमानोऽर्थः कुतो न विवक्ष्यते ।

with its subsidiary aṅgas and mystic doctrines,  they call a spiritual teacher (āchārya)." Now the teaching which is the function of the teacher cannot be fulfilled without the learning which is the function of the pupil,

विवक्षिते घ वेदार्ये यत्र यत्र पुरुषस्य संदेहः स सर्वोऽपि विचारशास्त्रस्य विषयो भविष्यति ।

and therefore the very injunction to teach implies and establishes a corresponding obligation to learn,  since the influencer's efforts fail without those of one to be influenced.

तनिर्णयच प्रयोजनम् ।

If you object that this view does not make reading the Veda the object of definite injunction,  I reply, What matters it to us if it is not?

तस्मादध्यापनविधिप्रयुक्तेनाध्ययनेनावगम्यमानस्यार्थस्य विचाराईत्वादिचार शास्त्रस्य वैधत्वेन विचारशास्त्रमारम्भणीयमिति राद्धान्तसंग्रहः।

[259] Therefore the former primâ facie argument and its answer,  which were given before under the idea that there was a definite injunction to read the Veda,

#### 8

स्यादेतत् ।

must now be discussed in another way to suit this new view.  Now the primâ facie argument was that the study of Mímāṃsā, not being authoritatively enjoined,

वेदस्य कथमपौरुषेयत्वमभिधीयते ।

is not to be commenced;  the "conclusion" was that it is to be commenced as being thus authoritatively enjoined.

तत्प्रतिपादकप्रमाणाभावात् ।

Now the upholders of the former or primâ facie view argue as follows: —"We put to the advocates of the conclusion the following dilemma:

अथ मन्येथा अपौरुषेया वेदाः संप्रदायाविच्छेदे सत्यस्मर्यमाणकर्तृः कत्वादात्मवदिति ।

Does the injunction to teach imply that the pupil is to understand the meaning of what is read,  or does it only refer to the bare reading?

तदेतन्मन्दम् ।

It cannot be the former,  for obviously the act of teaching cannot depend for its fulfilment on the pupil's understanding what is taught [as this will depend on his ability as a recipient]; and the latter will not help you,

विशेषणासिद्धः ।

as, if the bare reading is sufficient,  the Mímāṃsā discussions in question will have no subject or use.

पौरुषेयवेदवादिभिः प्रलये संप्रदायविच्छेदस्य कक्षीकरणात् ।

For their proper subject is a point in the Veda,  which is doubted about from having been only looked at in a rough and impromptu way;

किंच किमिदमस्मर्यमाणकर्तृकत्वं नामा: भीयमागकर्तकत्वमस्मरणगोचरकर्तकत्वं वा ।

now if there is no need of understanding the meaning at all,  why should we talk of doubts and still more of any hope of ascertaining the true meaning by means of laborious discussion?

न प्रथमः कल्पः ।

And therefore in accordance with the well-known principle,  'That which is a thing of use and not a matter of doubt is an object of attainment to an intelligent man,

परमेश्वरस्य कर्तुः प्रमितेरभ्युपगमात् ।

as, for instance,  a jar which is in broad light and in contact with the external and internal senses,'

न द्वितीयः ।

as there is in the present case no such thing as a subject to exercise it upon,  or a useful end to be attained by it,

विकल्पासहत्वात् ।

we maintain that the study of Mímāṃsā is not to be commenced."  We grant,

तथाहि\-किमेकेनास्मरणमभिप्रेयते सर्वैर्वा ।

in reply,  that the injunction to teach does not imply a corresponding necessity that the student must understand the meaning;

नाऽऽद्यः ।

still when a man has read the Veda with its subsidiary aṅgas,  and has comprehended the general connection of the words with their respective meanings,

यो धर्मशीलो जितमानरोष इत्यादिषु मुक्तकोक्तिषु व्यभिचारात् ।

this will imply an understanding of the meaning of the Veda,  just as it would in any ordinary human compositions.

न द्वितीयः ।

"But may we not say that,  just as in the case of the mother who said to her son,

सर्वास्मरणस्यासर्वज्ञदुर्बानत्वात् ।

'Eat poison,'  the meaning literally expressed by the words was not what she wished to convey,

पौरुषेयत्वे प्रमाणसंभवाच ।

since she really intended to forbid his eating anything at all in such and such a house;  so if the literal meaning of the Veda does not express its[187] real purport,

वेदवाक्यानि पौरुषेयाणि वाक्यत्वात्कालिदासादिवाक्यवत् ।

the old objection will recur with full force that the study of Mímāṃsā will have neither subject nor end [as there will be no use in understanding the literal meaning,  since, as in the mother's case,

वेदवाक्याँन्याप्तप्रणीतानि प्रमाणत्वे सति वाक्यत्वान्मन्वादिवा. क्यवदिति ।

it may only lead astray,  and so common sense must be the ultimate judge"]. We reply,

वेदस्याध्ययनं सर्व गुर्वध्ययनपूर्वकम् ।

that your supposed illustration and the case in question are not really parallel.  In the supposed illustration the primary meaning of the words would be obviously precluded,

वेदाध्ययनसामान्यादधुनाध्ययनं यथा ॥

because a direction to eat poison would be inconceivable in the mouth of an authoritative and trustworthy speaker like a mother,  and you would know at once that this could not be what she wished to say;

#### 9

. इत्यनुमानं प्रतिसाधनं प्रगल्भत इति चेत्तदपि न प्रमाणकोटि प्रवेष्टुमीष्टे ।

but in the case of the Veda,  which is underived from any personal author,

भारताध्ययनं सर्व गुर्वध्ययनपूर्वकम् ।

why should not the literal meaning be the one actually intended?  And it is just the doubts that arise,

#### 10

इत्याभाससमानयोगक्षेमत्वात् ।

as they occasionally will do,  in reference to this intended meaning,

ननु तत्र व्यासः कर्तेति स्मयते ।

which will be the proper "subject" of Mímāṃsā discussion;  and the settlement of these doubts will be its proper "end."

... को ह्यन्यः पुण्डरीकाक्षान्महाभारतकृद्भवेत् ।

Therefore,  whenever the true meaning of the Veda is not obtained[260] by that reading which is virtually prescribed by the authoritative injunction to a Brahman to teach,

इत्यादाविति चेत्तदसारम् ।

it will be a proper subject for systematic discussion;  and hence we hold that the study of Mímāṃsā is enjoined,

'ऋचः सामानि जज्ञिरे ।

and should be commenced. Would you maintain that they have no personal author because,

छन्दांसि जज्ञिरे तस्माय. जुस्तस्मादजायत ' (ते. आ० ३ । १२) इति पुरुषसूक्ते वेदस्य सर्तकतामतिपादनात् ।

although there is an unbroken line of tradition,  there is no remembrance of any author,

किंचानित्यः शब्दः सामान्यवत्त्वे सत्यस्मदादिब ोन्द्रियग्राह्यत्वाघटवत् ।

just as is the case with the soul"? [262] This argument is weak,  because the alleged characteristics [unbroken tradition,

नन्विदमनुमानं स एवायं गकार इति प्रत्यभिज्ञाप्रमाणप्रतिहतमिति चेत्तदतिफल्गु ।

&c. ] are not proved;  for those who hold the human origin of the Vedas maintain [188]that the line of tradition was interrupted at the time of the dissolution of the universe.

ठूनपुनर्जातकेशंदलितकुन्दादाविव प्रत्यभिज्ञायाः सामान्य विषयत्वेन बाधकत्वाभावात् ।

And, again,  what is meant by this assertion that the author is not remembered?

नन्वशरीरस्य परमेश्वरस्य तास्वादिस्थानाभावेन वर्णोधारणासंभवात्कथं तत्पणीतत्वं वेदस्य स्यादिति चेन्न तद्भद्रम् ।

Is it (1. ) that no author is believed,  or (2. ) that no author is remembered?

स्वभावतोऽभरीरस्यापि तस्य भक्तानुग्रहार्थं लीलाविग्रहग्रहणसंभवात् ।

The first alternative cannot be accepted,  since we hold that God is proved to have been the author.

तस्मादिस्यापौरुपेयर्ववाचोयुक्तिर्न युक्तेति चेत्तत्र समाधानमभिधीयते ।

Nor can the second,  because it cannot stand the test of the following dilemma,

किमिदं पौरुषेयस्वं सिषाधयिषितम् ।

viz. , is it meant (a. ) that no author of the Veda is remembered by some one person,  or (b. ) by any person whatever?

पुरुषादुत्पन्नत्वौत्रं यथाऽस्मदादिभिरहरहरुच्चार्यमाणस्य बंदस्य ।

[263] And the latter supposition is inadmissible,  since it would be impossible for any person who was not omniscient to know that no author of the Veda was recollected by any person whatever.

प्रमाणान्तरेणार्थमुपलभ्य तत्प्रकाशनाय रचितत्वं वा यथाऽस्मदादिभिरेव निबध्यमानस्य प्रबन्धस्य ।

Moreover,  there is actual proof that the Veda had a personal author,

प्रथमे न विप्रतिपत्तिः ।

for we argue as follows: —The sentences of the Veda must have originated from a personal author,

चरमे किमनुमानबलात्तत्साधनमागमबलाद्वा ।

since they have the character of sentences like those of Kālidāsa and other writers.  And, again,

नाऽऽद्यः ।

the sentences of the Veda have been composed by a competent person,  since, while they possess authority,

मालतीमाधवादिवाक्येषु सव्यभिचारस्वात् ।

they have,  at the same time,

अथ प्रमाणत्वे सतीति विशिष्यत इति चेत्तदपि न विपधितो मनसि वैशयमापद्यते ।

the character of sentences,  like those of Manu and other sages.

प्रमाणान्तरागोचरार्थपतिपादकं हि वाक्यं वेदवाक्यम् ।

But [ask the Mímāṃsakas] may it not be assumed that "all study of the Veda was preceded by an earlier study of it by the pupil's preceptor,  since the study of the Veda must always have had one common character which was the same in former times as now;"

व्याघातापातात् ।

and therefore this uninterrupted succession has force to prove the eternity of the Veda?  This reasoning,

... . किंच परमेश्वरस्य लीलाविग्रहपरिग्रहाभ्युपगमेऽप्यतीन्द्रियार्थदर्शनं न संजाघटीति ।

however [the Naiyāyikas [189]answer], cannot rise to the height of proof,  for it has no more validity than such obviously illusory reasoning,

देशकालस्वभावविप्रकृष्टार्थग्रहणोपायाभावात् ।

as "All study of the Mahābhārata was preceded by an earlier study of it by the pupil's preceptor,  since it is the study of the Mahābhārata,

न च तच्चक्षुरादिकमेवं तादृक्प्रतीतिजननक्षममिति मन्तव्यम् ।

which must have been the same in former times as now."  But [the Mímāṃsakas will ask whether there is not a difference between these two cases,

दृष्टानुसारेणैव कल्पनाया आश्रयणीयत्वात् ।

since] the Smṛiti declares that [Vishṇu incarnate as] Vyāsa was the author of the Mahābhārata,  in accordance with the line,

यत्राप्यतिशयो दृष्टः स स्वार्थानतिलङ्घनात् ।

"Who else than the lotus-eyed Vishṇu could be the maker of the Mahābhārata?"  [while nothing of this sort is recorded in any Smṛiti in regard to the Veda]. This argument,

दूरसूक्ष्मादिदृष्टौ स्यान्न रूपे श्रोत्रवृत्तिता ॥

however, is pithless,  since those words of the Purushasúkta (Rig V. , x. 90), "From him sprang the Ṛich and Sāman verses;

#### 11

अत एव नाऽऽगमबलात्तत्साधनम् ।

from him sprang the Metres;  from him the Yajus arose;"

यथा\-तेन प्रोक्तमिति ( पा० सू० ४ । ३ १०१) पाणिन्यनुशासने जाग्रत्यपि काठककालापतैत्तिरीयमित्यादिसमाख्याऽ. ध्ययनसंप्रदायप्रवर्तकविषयत्वेनोपपद्यते ।

prove that the Veda had a maker.  Further [proceed the Naiyāyikas] we hold that sound is non-eternal[264] because it has genus,

तद्वदत्रापि संप्रदायपवर्तकविषयत्वेनाप्युपपद्यते ।

and is also perceptible to the external organs of beings such as ourselves,  just as a jar is.

न चानुमानबलाच्छब्दस्यानित्यत्वसिद्धिः।

[265] "But,"  you may object,

प्रत्यभिज्ञाविरोधात् ।

"is not this argument refuted by the proof arising from the fact that we recognise the letter g (for example) as the same we have heard before?" "But [asks the Mímāṃsaka] how can the Veda have been uttered by the incorporeal Parameśvara,

न चासत्ययकत्वे सामान्यनिबन्धनं तदिति सांप्रतम् ।

who has no palate or other organs of speech,  and therefore cannot have pronounced the letters?"

सामान्यनिबन्धनत्वमस्य बलब द्वाधकोपनिपातादास्थीयते कचिद्वयभिचारदर्शनाद्वा ।

"This objection [190][answers the Naiyāyika] is not happy,  because, though Parameśvara is by nature incorporeal,

तत्र कचिद्वयभिचारदर्शने तदुत्प्रेक्षायामुक्तं स्वतःप्रामाण्यवादिभिः\- ... ।

he can yet assume a body in sport,  in order to show kindness to his worshippers.

उत्प्रेक्षेत हि यो मोहादज्ञातमपि बाधनम् ।

Consequently the arguments in favour of the doctrine that the Veda had no personal author are inconclusive."  I shall now [says the Mímāṃsaka] clear up the whole question.

स सर्वव्यवहारेषु संशयात्मा विनश्यति ॥

What is meant by this paurusheyatva ["derivation from a personal author"] which it is sought to prove?  Is it (1. ) mere procession (utpannatva) from a person,

#### 12

नन्विदं प्रत्यभिज्ञानं गत्वादिजातिविषयं ने गादिव्यक्तिविषयम् ।

like the procession of the Veda from persons such as ourselves,  when we daily utter it?

तासांप्रतिपुरुषं भेदोपलम्भात् ।

or (2. ) is it the arrangement— with a view to its manifestation—

अन्यथा सोमशर्माऽधीत इति विभागो न स्यादिति चेत्तदपि शोभा न बिभर्ति।

of knowledge acquired by other modes of proof,  as in the case of treatises composed by persons like ourselves?

गादिव्यक्तिभेदे प्रमाणाभावेन गत्वादिजातिविषयकल्पनाया प्रमाणाभावात् ।

If the first meaning be intended,  there will be no dispute between us.

यथों गोत्वमजानत एकमेव भिन्नदेशपरिमाणसंस्थानव्यक्त्गुपधानवशाद्भिन्नदेशमिवॉल्पमिव महादिव दीर्घमिव वामनमिव प्रथते तथा गव्यक्तिमजानत एकाऽपि व्यञ्जक भेदात्तत्तद्धर्मानुबन्धिनी प्रतिभासते ।

[266] If the second sense be meant,  I ask whether it is established (a. ) by inference,

एतेन विरुद्धधर्माध्यासाझेदसिद्धिरिति अत्युक्तम् ।

(a. ) The former alternative cannot be correct,  because your argument would equally apply to the sentences in dramas such as the Mālatímādhava [which,

तत्र किं स्वाभाविको विरुद्धधर्माध्यासो भेदसाधकत्वेनाभिमतः प्रातीतिको वा ।

of course,  being a work of fiction,

प्रथमेऽसिद्धिः।

has no authoritative character]. If you qualify your argument by inserting the saving clause,  "while they possess authority,"

अपरथा स्वाभाविकभेदाभ्युपगमे दश गकारादचारयच्चैत्र इति प्रतिपत्तिः स्यान्न तु दशकृत्वो गकार इति ।

[268] [as supra,  p. 188, line 21], even this explanation will fail to satisfy a philosopher.

द्वितीये तु न स्वाभाविकभेदसिद्धिः ।

For the sentences of the Veda are universally defined to be sentences which prove things that are not provable by other evidence.  But if you could establish that these Vedic sentences only prove what is provable by other evidence,

न हि परोपाधिभेदेन स्वाभाविकमक्यं विहन्यते ।

this definition would be at once [191]contradicted,  just as if a man were to say that his mother was a barren woman.

= मा भन्नभसोऽपि कुम्भाधुपाधिभेदात्स्वाभाविको भेदैः ।

And even if we granted that Parameśvara might assume a body in sport,  in order to show kindness to his worshippers,

तत्र व्यावृत्तव्यवहारो नादनिदानः ।

it would not at all follow that he would perceive things beyond the reach of the senses,  from the want of any means of apprehending objects removed from him in place,

\- प्रयोजनं तु यज्जातेस्तद्वर्णादेव \* लप्स्यते ।

in time, and in nature.  [269] Nor is it to be assumed that his eyes and other senses alone would have the power of producing such knowledge,

व्यक्तिलभ्यं तु नादेभ्य इति गत्वादिधीवृथा ॥

for we can only draw upon our imagination in accordance with our past experience.  This has been declared by the Guru [Prabhākara] when he refutes the supposition of an omniscient author—

#### 13

मत्यभिज्ञा यदा शब्दे जागर्ति निरवग्रहा।

"Wherever we do find the power of an organ intensified, [270] it is done without its going beyond its own proper objects;

अनित्यत्वानुमानानि सैव सर्वाणि बाधते ॥

thus it may appear in the power of seeing the very distant or the very minute,  but not in the ear's becoming cognisant of form."

#### 14

एतेनेदमपास्तं यदवादि वागीश्वरेण मानमनोहरे\-अनित्यः शब्द इन्द्रियग्राह्यविशेषगुणत्वाचक्षुरूपवदिति ।

Hence (b. ) we also maintain that your position cannot be established by any supposed supernatural testimony [as that quoted above from the Rig-Veda,  "from him sprang the Ṛich and Sāman verses"]. For the rule of Pāṇini (iv.

शब्दद्रव्यत्ववादिनं प्रत्यसिद्धः ।

, though we maintain that these names have reference [not to those parts of the Veda as first composed by these sages,  but] to the fact that these sages instituted certain schools of traditional study.

ध्वन्यंशे सिद्धसाधनत्वाच्च ।

And in the same way we hold [in reference to this verse from the Rig-Veda] that it only refers to the institution of certain schools of traditional study of these Vedas.  Nor will any supposed inference establish the non-eternity [192]of sound,

अश्रावणवोपाधिबाधितत्वाच्च ।

because [as we said before] it is opposed to the evidence of our consciousness,  [since we certainly recognise the letter now heard as the one heard before]. Nor is it reasonable to reply that,

= इत आरभ्य यज्जातेरित्यन्तो ग्रन्थो घ. पुस्तके न विद्यते।

although the letters are not the same,  they seem to be so on account of their identity of species.

\* घ. पु. टि.\-\-ततः स्वाभाविकमैक्यं वर्णादेव।

For here we ask our opponents a question— Is this idea that "the apparent sameness arises from identity of species" put forward from a wish to preclude entirely any idea of the letters being the same,

\-\- शब्द इति व्यवहाराचरणे कारणं प्रत्यक्षं शब्दानित्यत्वे प्रमाणयति स्म ।

or only [from an imagined fear of error] because experience shows that the recognition will sometimes be erroneous [as in the cases of the hair and jasmine mentioned above]? (a. ) If it arises from the latter reason,  we Mímāṃsakas,

सोऽपि विरुद्धधर्मसंसर्गस्यौपाधिकत्वोपपादनन्यायेन दत्तरक्तबलिवेतालसमः ।

who hold that the Veda is its own evidence,  have said in reference to this timid imagination—

यो हि नित्यत्वे सर्वदोपलब्ध्यनुपलब्धिप्रसङ्गो न्यायभूषणकारोक्तः सोऽपि ध्वनिसंस्कृतस्योपलम्भाभ्युपगमात्प्रतिक्षिप्तः ।

"He who foolishly imagines that something as yet unknown to him will come hereafter to stop his present conclusion,  will go to utter ruin in every transaction of life,

यत्तुं युगपदिन्द्रियसंबन्धित्वेन प्रतिनियतसंस्कारकसंस्कार्यत्वाभावानुमानं तदात्मन्यनैकान्तिमित्यलमतिकलहेन ।

his mind a mass of doubts."  (b. ) "But [the Naiyāyikas will ask] does not this recognition of g and other letters [as the same which we heard before] refer to the species which exists the same in each,

ततश्च वेदस्यापौरुषेयतया निरस्तसमस्तशङ्काकलङ्कगफूरत्वेन स्वतःसिद्धं धर्मे प्रामाण्यामिति सुस्थितम् ।

and not to the several individual letters,  since, in fact,

स्यादेतत् ।

we perceive that they are different as uttered by different persons,  otherwise we could not make such distinctions as we do when we say 'Somaśarman is reading'?" This objection,

प्रमाणत्वाप्रमाणत्वे स्वतः सांख्याः समाश्रिताः।

however, has as little brilliancy as its predecessors,  for as there is no proof of any distinction between the individual g's, there is no proof that we ought to assume any such thing as a species g; and we maintain that,

.. नैयायिकास्ते पर: सौगताश्चरमं स्वतः ॥

just as to the man who does not understand [the Naiyāyika doctrine of] the species g, the one species [in the Naiyāyika view] will by the influence of distinction of place,  magnitude,

#### 15

प्रथमं परतः पाहुः प्रामाण्यं वेदवादिनः ।

form, and individual sounds,  appear as if it were variously modified as itself distinct in place,

प्रमाणत्वं स्वतः माहुः परतश्चाप्रमाणताम् ।

as small,  as great,

#### 16

इति षादिविवाददर्शनात्कथंकारं स्वतःसिद्धं धर्म प्रामाण्यमिति सिद्धवत्कृत्य स्वी क्रियते ।

as long, as short;  so to the man who does not understand our [Mímāṃsaka doctrine of] one individual[193] g, the one g (in our view) will by the diversity of "manifesters,"

किंच किमिदं स्वतः प्रामाण्यं नाम ।

[271] appear to him associated with their respective peculiarities;  and as contrary characters are in this way ascribed [to the letter g], there is a fallacious appearance of distinction [between different g's]. But does this ascription of contrary characters,

किं स्वत एव प्रामाण्यस्य जन्म ।

which is thus regarded as creating a difference [between the g's], result (1. ) from the nature of the thing, There is no proof of the former alternative;

आहोस्वित्स्वाश्रयज्ञानजन्यत्वम् ।

for, if it were true,  as an inherent difference would have to be admitted between different g's, we should have to say,

किमुत स्वाश्रयज्ञानसामग्रीजन्यत्वम् ।

"Chaitra has uttered ten g's," and not "Chaitra has uttered the same g ten times."  On the latter supposition,

उताहो ज्ञानसामग्रीजन्यज्ञानविशेषाश्रितत्वम् ।

there is no proof of any inherent distinction between g's, for inherent oneness is not destroyed by a difference of external disguises.  Thus we must not conceive,

किंवा ज्ञानसामान्यसामग्रीमात्रजन्यज्ञानविशेषाश्रितत्वम् ।

from the apparent distinction caused by such external disguises as jars,  &c. , that there is any inherent distinction,

तत्राऽऽद्यः सावधः ।

as of parts,  in the one indivisible ether.

कार्यकारणभावस्य भेदसमानाधिकरणत्वेनैकस्मिन्नसंभवात् ।

The current use of the rejected phrase [i. e. , "different" as applied to the g's] is really caused by the noise,  which in each case is different.

नापि द्वितीयः ।

This has been said by the great teacher— "The object which the Naiyāyikas seek by supposing a species is,

गुणस्य सतो ज्ञानस्य प्रामाण्यं प्रति समवायिकारणतया द्रव्यत्वापातात् ।

in fact, gained from the letter itself;  and the object which they aim at by supposing an individuality in letters,

नापि तृतीयः।

is attained from audible noises; [272] so that the assumption of species is useless."

प्रामाण्यस्योपाधित्वे जातित्वे वा जन्मायोगात् ।

And again— "Since in regard to sounds such an irresistible instinct of recognition is always awake within us,

स्मृतित्वानधिकरणस्य ज्ञानस्य बाधा. त्यन्ताभावः प्रामाण्योपाधिः ।

it precludes by its superior evidence all the inferences to prove sound's non-eternity."  This at once refutes the argument given in the [Naiyāyika] [194]treatise by Vāgíśwara,

न च तस्योत्पत्तिसंभवः ।

entitled Māna-manohara,  "sound is non-eternal from the fact of its being a special quality belonging to an organ of sense[273] (sc.

अत्यन्ताभावस्य नित्यत्वाभ्युपगमात् ।

the ear), just as colour is to the eye."  We can also refute it in the following ways:

अत एव न जातेरपि जनियुज्यते ।

) if we take it as referring to the noise,  not the sound,

नापि चतुर्थः ।

we have no dispute,  as it only establishes what we ourselves allow;

ज्ञानविशेषो ह्यपी ।

and (c. ) the inference is overthrown by the "limiting condition" [upādhi] of aśrāvaṇatva,  or "the not causing audition."

विशेषसामय्यां च सामान्यसामयनुपविशति शिशपासाम ध्यामिव वृक्षसामग्री ।

[275] So Udayana tries at great length to establish that,  although ether,

\* अपरथा +तस्याऽऽकस्मिकत्वं प्रसज्येत ।

the site of sound,  is imperceptible,

तस्मात् =परतस्त्वेन स्वीकृताप्रामाण्य विज्ञानसामान्यसामग्रीजन्याश्रितमित्यतिव्याप्तिरापद्यत ।

the non-existence of that which abides in this site is perceptible;  and he then brings forward as an evidence for the non-eternity of sound,

पश्चमविकल्पं विकल्पयामः।

that sense perception which causes the use of such common expressions as "The tumult is stopped,"  "The sound has arisen."

किं दोपाभावसहकृतज्ञानसामग्रीजन्य॑त्वमेव ज्ञानसामग्रीमात्रजन्यस्वं किंवा दोषाभावासहकृतज्ञानसामग्रीजन्यत्वम् ।

[276] But he is sufficiently answered[277] by our old reply [in p. 193], that the fallacious appearance of [195]distinction arises from contrary characters being erroneously ascribed,  just as, in the story,

नाऽऽयः। दोपाभावसहकृतमानसामग्रीजन्यत्वमेव परतः प्रामाण्यमिति परतःप्रामाण्यवादिभिरुररीकरणात् ।

the demon Tāla went away [as well as Betāla] when the offering of blood was given to the latter.  [278] And as for the objection raised by the author of the Nyāyabhúshaṇa,[279] that,

नापि द्वितीयः ।

if sound were eternal,  the conclusion must follow that it would be either always perceptible or always imperceptible,

दोषाभावसहकृतत्वेन सामग्यां सहकृतत्वे सिद्धेऽनन्यथासिद्धान्वयव्यतिरेकसिद्धतया दोषाभावस्य कारणताया वज्रलेपायमानत्वात् ।

this also is obviated by our allowing that we only perceive that sound which is manifested by our articulate noise.  [280] And as for the (Naiyāyika) argument against the existence[281] of such a constant relation as this which is supposed between the manifested "sound" and the manifesting "noise,"

अभावः कारणमेव न भवतीति चेत्तदा वक्तव्यमभावस्य कार्यत्वमस्ति न वा ।

since they both come simultaneously in contact with the sense of hearing,  this is invalid,

यदि नास्ति तदा पटमध्वं लानुपपत्या पटस्य नित्यताप्रसङ्गः ।

as it will indisputably apply with equal force in the case of the soul. Therefore as the Veda is thus proved to have not originated from any personal author,

अथास्ति किमपराद्धं कारणत्वेनेति सेयमुभयतःपाशा रज्जुः।

and as the minutest germ of suspicion against it is thus absolutely destroyed,  we hold it as satisfactorily demonstrated that it has a self-established authority in all matters relating to duty.

तदुदितमुदयनेन\- भावो यथा तथाऽभावः कारणं कार्यवन्मतः ॥

"Well"[283] [say our opponents], "let this question rest;  [196]but how about another well-known controversy?

#### 17

(न्या०कु०१।१०) इति ।

It is said— "'The Sāṅkhyas hold that both authoritativeness and non-authoritativeness are self-proved;

तथाच प्रयोगः\-विमतं प्रमाण्यं ज्ञानहेत्वतिरिक्तहेत्वधीनं कार्यत्वे सति तद्विशेपाश्रितत्वादप्रामाण्यवेत् ।

the followers of the Nyāya hold that both are proved by something else [as inference,  &c. ]; the Buddhists hold that the latter is self-proved and the former proved by something else;

प्रामाण्यं परतो ज्ञायतेऽनभ्यासदशायां सांशयिकत्वादप्रामाण्यवत् ।

the teachers of the Veda maintain that authoritativeness is self-proved and non-authoritativeness proved by something else.  ' Now we ask,

तस्मादुत्पत्तौ ज्ञप्तौ च परतस्त्वे प्रमाणसंभवात्स्वतः सिद्धं भामाण्यमित्येतत्पूतिकूष्माण्डायत इति चेत्तदेतदाकाशमुष्टिहननायते ।

amidst all this discussion,  how do the Mímāṃsakas accept as established their tenet that the authoritativeness of duty is self-proved?

विज्ञानसामग्रीजन्यत्वे सति ।

Is it (a. ) that authoritativeness springs from itself?  or (b. ) that it springs from the right knowledge in which it resides?

तदतिरिक्तहेत्वजन्यत्वं प्रमायाः स्वतस्त्वमिति निरुक्तिसंभवात् ।

or (c. ) that it springs from the instrumental causes [as the eye,  &c. ] which produced the right knowledge in which it resides?

अस्ति चात्रानुमानम् ।

or (d. ) that it resides in a particular knowledge produced by the instrumental causes which produced the right knowledge?  [284] or (e. ) that it resides in a particular knowledge produced by the instrumental causes only which produced the right knowledge?

विमता प्रमा विज्ञानसामग्रीजन्यत्वे सति तदतिरिकजन्या न भवति अप्रमात्वानधिकरणत्वात् ।

e. , authoritativeness cannot cause itself]. (b. ) It cannot be the second,  because if knowledge,

घटादिप्रमावत् ।

which is a quality,  were the cause of authoritativeness,

न चौद. यनमनुमानं परतस्त्वसाधकमिति शङ्कनीयम् ।

it would have to be a substance,  as being an intimate cause.

\* घ. पु. टि.\- अपरथा विशेषसामग्न्यनङ्गीकारे ।

[285] (c. ) It cannot be the third,  because 'authoritativeness' cannot properly be [197]'produced' at all,

+ घ. पु. टि.\- तस्य विशेषविज्ञानस्य ।

[286] whether we call it a general characteristic (upādhi) or a species (jāti);[287] for if we call it an upādhi,  it is defined as the absolute non-existence of any contradiction to a certain kind of knowledge which does not possess the nature of recollection;

घ. पु. टि.\-सामान्यसामग्यतिरिक्तविशेषसामग्रीजन्याश्रितत्वं परतस्त्वम् ।

[288] and this cannot be produced,  for we all allow that absolute non-existence is eternal;

.. इत आरभ्य सति इत्यन्तो प्रन्थः व. पुस्तके नास्ति ।

and still less can we speak of its being produced,  if we regard it as a species.

ग्रीमात्रादेव प्रमोत्पत्ति संभवे तदतिरिक्तस्य गुणस्य दोषाभावस्य वा कारणत्वकल्पनायां कल्पनागौरवप्रसङ्गाच्च ।

(d. ) Nor can it be the fourth,  for wrong knowledge [as well as right knowledge] is a particular kind of knowledge,

ननु दोषस्याप्रपाहेतुत्वेन तदभावस्य प्रेम प्रति हेतुत्वं दुर्निवारमिति चेन्न ।

and the instrumental causes which produce the general are included in those which produce the particular, [289] just as the general idea 'seed,'

दोषाभावस्याप्रमाप्रतिबन्धकत्वेनान्यथासिद्धत्वात् ।

as applied to 'tree,'  is included in the particular seed of any special tree,

तस्माद्गुणेभ्यो दोषाणामभावस्तदभावतः ।

as, e. g. , the Dalbergia Sisu;  otherwise we might suppose that the particular had no instrumental cause at all.

अप्रामण्यद्वय सत्त्वं तेनोत्सर्गो नयोदितः || इति ।

Your definition would therefore extend too far [and include erroneous as well as true knowledge]; for non-authoritativeness,  which Vedantists and most Mímāṃsakas allow to be produced by something external,

तथा प्रमाज्ञप्तिरपि ज्ञानज्ञापकसामग्रीत एव जायते ।

(e. ) As for your fifth view,  we ask whether by being produced by the instrumental causes only which produced right knowledge,

न च संशयानुदयमसङ्गने बाधक इति युक्तं वक्तुम् ।

you mean to include or exclude the absence of a 'defect'? It cannot be the former alternative;  because the followers of the Nyāya who hold that authoritativeness is proved by something external [as inference,

सत्यपि प्रतिभासपुष्कलकारणे प्रतिबन्धकदोघादिसमवर्धनात्तदुपपत्तेः ।

&c. ], would at once grant that authoritativeness is produced by the instrumental causes of knowledge combined with the absence of a 'defect.  ' [198]Neither can it be the latter alternative;

किंच तावकमनुमानं स्वतः प्रमाणं न वा ।

for, inasmuch as it is certain that the absence of a 'defect' is found combined with the various instrumental causes,  this absence of a 'defect' is fixed as by adamantine glue to be a cause of right knowledge,

आधेनैकान्तिकता | द्वितीये तस्यापि परतः प्रामाण्यमेवं तस्य तस्यापीत्यनवस्था दुरवस्था स्यात् ।

since right knowledge will always accompany its presence,  and be absent if it is absent,

यदत्र कुसुमाञ्जल|बुदयनेन झटिति चुरप्रवृत्तेः प्रामाण्यनिश्चया श्रीनत्वामावमापादयता प्रण्यगादिं ।

[290] and it will at the same time be not an unimportant condition.  [291] If you object that non-existence (or absence) cannot be a cause,

प्रवृत्तिहींच्छामपेक्षते ।

we reply by asking you whether non-existence can be an effect or not?  If it cannot,

तत्प्राचुर्य चेच्छाप्राचुर्यम् ।

then we should have to allow that cloth is eternal,  as its "emergent non-existence" or destruction would be impossible.

इच्छा चेष्टसाधनताज्ञानम् ।

If it can be an effect,  then why should it not be a cause also?

तच्चेष्टजातीयत्वलिङ्गनुभवम् ।

So this rope binds you at both ends.  This has also been said by Udayana [in his Kusumāñjali,

सोऽपीन्द्रियार्थसंनिकर्षम् | प्रामाण्यग्रहणं तु न क्वचिदुपयुज्यत इति ।

"'As existence,  so too non-existence is held to be a cause as well as an effect.

तदपि तस्करस्य पुरस्ताकक्षे सुवर्णमुपेत्य सर्वाङ्गोद्घाटनमिव प्रतिभाँति ।

"The argument,  in my opinion,

यतः समीहितसाधनताज्ञानमेव प्रमाणैतयाऽवगम्यमानमिच्छां जनयतीत्यत्रैत्र स्फुट एव प्रामाण्यग्रहणस्वोपयोगः ।

runs as follows: —Right knowledge depends on some cause[292] other than the common causes of knowledge,

किंच क्वचिदपि चेन्निर्विचिकित्सा प्रवृत्तिः संशयादपपद्येत तर्हि सर्वश्र तथाभाव संभवात्प्रामाण्यनिश्चयो निरर्थकः स्यात् ।

from the very fact that,  while it is an effect,

तथोक्तम् \- अनिश्चितस्य सत्वमेव दुर्लभमिति ।

it is also knowledge,  just as wrong knowledge does.

तस्माद्धर्मे स्वतःसिद्धप्रमाणभाव ज्योतिष्टोमन स्वर्गकामो यजेतेत्यादिविध्यवादमननामधेयात्मके वेदे यजेतेत्यत्र प्रत्ययः प्रकृत्यर्थोपरक्तां भावनामाभिपत्त इति सिद्ध व्युत्पत्तिमभ्युपगच्छनामभिहितान्वयवादिनां भट्टाचार्याणां सिद्धान्तः ।

g. , inference], because doubt arises in regard to it in an unfamiliar case,  as we also see in non-authoritativeness.

यागविषयं नियोगामिति कार्ये व्युत्पत्तिमनुसरतामन्विताभिधानबादिनां प्रभाकरगुरूणां सिद्धान्त इति सर्वमवदातम् ।

"Therefore,  as we can prove that authoritativeness is both produced and recognised by means of something external,

#### 18

## c13

#### 0

अथ पाणिनिदर्शनम् ॥

THE PāṆINI-DARŚANA.

#### 1

नवयं प्रकृतिभागोऽयं प्रत्ययभाग इति प्रकृतिप्रत्ययविभागः कथमवगम्यत इति चेत्पीतपातञ्जलजलानामेतच्चाद्यं चमत्कारं न करोति ।

If any one asks,

व्याकरणशास्त्रस्य प्रकृतिप्रत्ययविभागप्रतिपादनपरतायाः प्रसिद्धत्वात् ।

"Where are we to learn how to separate a root and an affix so as to be able to say,

तथाहि\-पतञ्जलेभंगवतो महाभाष्यकारस्येदमादिमं वाक्यम्\-अथ शब्दानुशासनमिति (पात० म० भा० शश१)।

'This part is the original root and this is an affix,'"

अस्यार्थी\-अथेत्ययं शब्दोऽधिकारार्थः प्रयुज्यते ।

may we not reply that to those who have drunk the waters of Patañjali this question produces no confusion,

अधिकारः प्रस्तावः ।

since it is notorious that the rules of grammar have reference to this very point of the separation of the original roots and affixes?

प्रारम्भ इति यावत् ।

Thus the very first sentence of the venerable Patañjali,

शब्दानुशासनशब्देन च पाणिनिप्रणीतं व्याकणशास्त्रं विवक्ष्यते ।

the author of the "Great Commentary,"

शब्दानुशासनमित्येतापत्यभिधीयमाने संदेहः स्यात् ।

is "atha śabdānuśāsanam,"

किं शब्दानुशासनं प्रस्तूयते न वेति ।

"Now comes the exposition of words."

तथा मा प्रसाङ्गीदित्यथशब्दं पायुक्त ।

The particle atha ("now") is used here as implying a new topic or a commencement;

अर्थशब्दप्रयोगवलेनार्थान्तरव्युदासेन प्रस्तूयत इत्यस्यार्थस्याभिधीयमानत्वात् ।

and by the phrase,

अनेन हि वैदिकाः शब्दाः 'शं नो देवीरभिष्टये' ( अ० सं० १ । १ ) इत्यादयस्तदुपकारिणी लौकिकाः शब्दा गौरश्वः पुरुषो हस्ती शकुनिरित्यादयः भानुशिष्यन्ते व्युत्पाद्य संस्क्रियन्ते प्रकृतिप्रत्ययविभागवत्तया बोध्यन्त इति शब्दानुशासनम् ।

"exposition of words,"

अत्र केचित्पर्यनुयुञ्जते\-अनुशासिक्रियायाः सकर्मकत्वात्कर्मभूतस्य शब्दस्य कर्तृभूतस्याऽऽचार्यस्य प्राप्तौ सत्यामुभयप्राप्तौ कणि (पा० सू० २ । ३ । ६६) इत्यनुशासनबलात्कर्मण्येषा षष्ठी विधातव्या ।

is meant the system of grammar put forth by Pāṇini.

तथा च कर्मणि चेति (पा० सू० २ । २ । १४ ) समासप्रतिषेधसंभवाच्छब्दानुशासनशब्दो न प्रमाणपथमवतरतीति ।

Now a doubt might here arise as to whether this phrase implies that the exposition of words is to be the main topic or not;

अत्रायं समाधिरभिधीयते\-योस्मन्कृत्मत्यये कर्तकर्मणो. रुभयोः प्राप्तिरस्ति तत्र कर्मण्येव षष्ठी विभक्तिर्भवति न कर्तरीति बहुव्रीहि. विज्ञानबलान्नियम्यते ।

and it is to obviate any such doubt that he employed the particle atha,

तद्यथाऽऽश्चर्यो गवां दोहोऽशिक्षितेन गोपालकेनति ।

since this particle implies that what follows is to be treated as the main topic to the exclusion of everything else.

कर्तपि षष्ठी भवतीति केचिद्रूवते ।

The word "exposition" (anuśāsana), as here used,

अत एवोक्तं काशिकावृत्तौ\-केचिदवि. शेषेणैव विभाषामिच्छन्ति शब्दानामनुशासनमाचार्येणाऽऽचार्यस्य वेति ।

implies that thereby Vaidic words,

शब्दानुशासनमित्यत्र तु शब्दानामनुशासनं नार्थानामित्येतावतो विवक्षित. स्थार्थस्याऽऽचार्यस्य कर्तुरुपादानेन विनाऽपि सुप्रतिपादत्वादाचार्योपादानमकिंचित्करम् ।

such as those in the line śaṃ no devír abhishṭaye,

तस्मादुभयप्राप्तेरभावादुभयप्राप्तौ कर्मणीत्येषा षष्ठी न भवति ।

[308] &c. , and secular words as ancillary to these,

किंतु कर्तृकर्मणोः कृतीति ( पा० सू० २ । ३ । ६५) कृयोगे कर्तरि कर्मणि च षष्टी विभक्तिर्भवतीति कृयोगलक्षणा पष्ठी भविष्यति ।

as the common words for "cow,"

तथा चेमप्रवश्वनपलाशशातनादिवत्समासो भविष्यति ।

"horse," "man,"

अथवा शेषलक्षणेयं षष्ठी ।

[204]"elephant,"

तत्र किमपि चोद्यं नावतरत्येव ।

"bird," &c. , are made the subject of the exposition,

यद्येवं तर्हि शेषलक्षणायाः षष्ठयाः सर्वत्र मुंवचत्वात्षष्ठीसमासप्रतिषेधसूत्राणामानर्थक्यं प्राप्नुयादिति चेत्सत्यम् ।

i. e. , are deduced from their original roots and properly formed,

तेषां स्वरचिन्तायामुपयोगो वाक्यपदीय हरिणा प्रादार्शि ।

or, in other words,

लौकिकव्यवहारेषु यथेष्टं चेष्टता जनः ।

are explained as divided into root and affix.

#### 2

इति पाणिनिसूत्रोंणामर्थवत्त्वमसौ यतः ।

We must consider that the compound in this phrase represents a genitive of the object [śabdānuśāsanam standing for śabdasyānuśāsanam], and as there is a rule of Pāṇini (karmaṇi cha,

जनिकतुरिति ब्रूते तत्प्रयोजक इत्यपि ॥

ii. 2, 14), which prohibits composition in such a construction,

#### 3

तथा न शब्दानुशासनापरनामधेयं व्याकरणशास्त्रमारचं वेदितव्यमिति वाक्यार्थः संपद्यते ।

we are forced to concede that the phrase śabdānuśāsanam does not come before us as a duly authorised compound.

तस्यार्थस्य झटिति प्रतिपत्तयेऽथ व्याकरणमित्येवाभिधीयताम् ।

Here, however,

अथ शब्दानुशासनमित्यधिकारिं मुधोऽभिधीयत इति ।

arises a discussion [as to the true application of the alleged rule of Pāṇini], for we hold that,

मैवम् । शब्दानुशासनमित्यन्वर्थसमाख्योपादाने वदीयवेदाङ्गत्वप्रतिपादकप्रयोजनान्वाख्यानसिः।

[310] Thus we must say,

अन्यथा प्रयोजनानभिधाने व्याकरणाध्ययनेऽध्येतृणां प्रवृत्तिरेव न सजेत् ।

"Wonderful is the milking of cows by an unpractised cowherd."

___ \* इत आरभ्य प्रयोजनानभिधान इत्यन्तो ग्रन्थो घ. पुस्तके न विद्यते ।

We may, however,

सेत्स्यतीति चेन्मैवम् ।

remark in passing that some authors do maintain that the agent may in such cases be put in the genitive (as well as the object); hence we find it stated in the Kāśikā Commentary:

तथा विधानेऽपि तदीयवेदाङ्गन्त्वप्रतिपादक प्रयोजनानभिधाने तेषां प्रवृत्तेरनुपपत्तेः ।

"Some authors maintain that there should be an option in such cases without any distinction,

तथाहि \- पुरा किल वेदमधीत्या ध्येतारस्त्वरितं वक्तारो भवन्ति ।

and thus they would equally allow such a construction as 'the exposition of words of the teacher' or 'by the teacher.

वेदान्नो वैदिकाः शब्दाः सिद्धा लोकाच्च लौकिकाः ।

'" Inasmuch,

तस्मादनर्थकं व्याकरणमिति ।

however, as the words of the phrase in question really mean that the "exposition" intended relates to words and not to things,

तस्माद्देदाङ्गत्वं मन्यमानास्तदध्ययने प्रवृत्तिम कार्षुः ।

and since this can be at once understood without any mention of the [205]agent,

ततश्चेदानींतनानामपि तत्र प्रवृत्तिर्न सिध्येत् ।

i. e. , the teacher,

सा मा प्रसाङ्क्षीदिति तदीयवेदाङ्गत्वनतिपादकं प्रयोजनमन्वाख्येयमेव ।

any such mention would be plainly superfluous;

यद्यन्वाख्याते प्रयोजने न वर्तेरंस्तर्हि लौकिकशब्द संस्कारज्ञानरहितास्ते याज्ञे कर्मणि प्रत्यवायभाजो भवेयुः ।

and therefore as the object and the agent are not both expressed in one and the same sentence,

धर्माद्धीयेरन् ।

this is not an instance of the genitive of the object (coming under ii.

अत एव याज्ञिकाः पठन्ति – आहिताग्निरपशब्दं प्रयुज्य प्रायश्चित्तीयां सारस्वतीमिष्टिं निर्वपेदिति ।

3, 66, and ii.

अतस्तदीयवेदाङ्गत्वमतिपादकप्रयोजनान्वाख्यानार्थमथ शब्दानुशासनमित्येव कथ्यते नाथ व्याक रणमिति ।

, ii. 3, 65, which directs that an agent or an object,

भवति च शब्द संस्कारो व्याकरणशास्त्रस्य प्रयोजनम् ।

in connection with a word ending with a kṛit affix,

तस्य तदुद्देशेन प्रवृत्तेः ।
